<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The endocrine system is made up of <strong>glands</strong> that <strong>produce</strong> that <strong>secrete hormones</strong>. Hormones are chemical messagers.</li>
<li>The main function of the system is enabling the body to <strong>communicate and coordinate</strong> other body systems to maintain balance, homeostasis, reproduction, growth and development and respond to external stress and injury.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<p>NB/There are two types of glands:
Endocrine glands
Exocrine glands</p>
<p>What are their differences?</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NED</p>
<p>Differences between endocrine and exocrine glands</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endocrine-glands">Endocrine Glands<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endocrine-glands" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Secrete into the internal environment.</li>
<li>No ducts</li>
<li>Secrete hormones</li>
<li>Minority</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="exocrine-glands">Exocrine Glands<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exocrine-glands" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Secrete into the external environment.</li>
<li>Have ducts</li>
<li>Secrete other stuff (sweat, oil, wax, enzymes, saliva, milk etc.)</li>
<li>Majority</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
BUREAU VERITAS 1828</p>
<p>The endocrine glands are the ones that make up the endocrine system. They include hormones produced by the;</p>
<ol>
<li>Hypothalamus:7</li>
<li>Pituitary gland: Primarily 7</li>
<li>Thyroid gland:2</li>
<li>Parathyroid glands:1</li>
<li>Pancreas: Primarily 2</li>
<li>Adrenal glands:3 types</li>
<li>Ovaries: Primarily 2</li>
</ol>

<p>Table 9.1 Hormones of the hypothalamus, anterior pituitary and their target tissues</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Hypothalamus</th><th>Anterior pituitary</th><th>Target gland or tissue</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>GHRH</td><td>GH</td><td>Most tissues</td></tr><tr><td>Many organs</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>GHRIH</td><td>GH inhibition</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>TSH inhibition</td><td>Thyroid gland</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Pancreatic islets</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Most tissues</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>TRH</td><td>TSH</td><td>Thyroid gland</td></tr><tr><td>CRH</td><td>ACTH</td><td>Adrenal cortex</td></tr><tr><td>PRH</td><td>PRL</td><td>Breast</td></tr><tr><td>PIH</td><td>PRL inhibition</td><td>Breast</td></tr><tr><td>LHRH or</td><td>FSH</td><td>Ovaries and testes</td></tr><tr><td>GnRH</td><td>LH</td><td>Ovaries and testes</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>JAWEMAN NATIONAL UNIVERSITY</p>
<p>GHRH = growth hormone releasing hormone
GH = growth hormone (somatotrophin)
GHRIH = growth hormone release inhibiting hormone (somatostatin)
TRH = thyrotrophin releasing hormone
TSH = thyroid stimulating hormone
CRH = corticotrophin releasing hormone
ACTH = adrenocorticotropic hormone
PRH = prolactin releasing hormone
PRL = prolactin (lactogenic hormone)
PIH = prolactin inhibiting hormone (dopamine)
LHRH = luteinising hormone releasing hormone
GnRH = gonadotrophin releasing hormone</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-pituitary">The pituitary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-pituitary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Located in sella turcica (hypophyseal fossa) of the sphenoid bone below the hypothalamus attached by a stalk.</li>
<li>It consists of two main parts (lobes):</li>
<li>☑ Anterior pituitary (adenohypophysis)</li>
<li>☑ Posterior pituitary (neurohypophysis).</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-pituitary">The Pituitary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-pituitary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="two-divisions">Two divisions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#two-divisions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Anterior pituitary (adenohypophysis)</li>
</ul>
<p>Pituitary secretes 9 hormones</p>
<ol>
<li>TSH</li>
<li>ACTH</li>
<li>FSH</li>
<li>LH</li>
<li>GH</li>
<li>PRL</li>
<li>MSH</li>
</ol>
<p>The first four are “tropic” hormones, they regulate the function of other hormones</p>
<ul>
<li>Posterior pituitary (neurohypophysis)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="8">
<li>ADH (antidiuretic hormone), or vasopressin</li>
<li>Oxytocin</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>BUREAU VERITAS 1828</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypothalamus-controls-anterior-pituitary-hormone-release">Hypothalamus controls anterior pituitary hormone release<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypothalamus-controls-anterior-pituitary-hormone-release" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Releasing hormones (releasing factors)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>i. TRH(thyroid releasing hormone)--- release of TSH</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>ii. CRH(corticotropin releasing hormone)---ACTH</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>iii. GnRH (=LHRH)-- FSH and LH</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>iv. PRF(prolactin releasing factor---cause release of PRL</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>v. GHRH( gonadotropin releasing hormone)--- GH release</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inhibiting hormones</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>i. PIF---inhibit Prolactin production</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>ii. GH inhibiting hormone ---inhibit GH production.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>BUREAU VERITAS 1828</p>
<p>The others from the anterior pituitary...</p>
<ul>
<li>GH (somatrotropic hormone) stimulates growth of skeletal epiphyseal plates and body to synthesize protein</li>
<li>PRL stimulates mammary glands in breast to make milk</li>
<li>MSH stimulates melanocytes; may increase mental alertness</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypersecretion-of-anterior-pituitary-hormones">Hypersecretion of anterior pituitary hormones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypersecretion-of-anterior-pituitary-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The most common cause is prolonged hypersecretion of growth hormone (GH), usually by a hormone-secreting pituitary tumour.</li>
<li>The conditions are occasionally due to excess growth hormone releasing hormone (GHRH) secreted by the hypothalamus.</li>
<li>As the tumour increases in size, compression of nearby structures may lead to hyposecretion of other pituitary hormones (from both lobes) and damage to the optic nerves, causing visual disturbances.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NED</p>
<p>The effects of excess GH include:</p>
<ul>
<li>excessive growth of bones</li>
<li>enlargement of internal organs</li>
<li>formation of excess connective tissue</li>
<li>enlargement of the heart and raised blood pressure</li>
<li>reduced glucose tolerance and a predisposition to diabetes mellitus.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gigantism">Gigantism.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gigantism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>occurs in children when there is excess GH while epiphyseal cartilages of long bones are still growing,</li>
<li>i.e. before ossification of bones is complete. It is evident mainly in the bones of the limbs, and</li>
<li>affected individuals may grow to heights of 2.1 to 2.4 m, although body proportions remain normal</li>
<li>abnormally high linear growth due to excessive action of insulin like growth factor I (IGF-I) while the epiphyseal growth plates are open during childhood</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acromegaly">Acromegaly.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acromegaly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This means ‘large extremities’ and occurs in adults when there is excess GH after ossification is complete.</li>
<li>The bones become abnormally thick and there is also thickening of the soft tissues.</li>
<li>These changes are most noticeable as coarse facial features but occurs after the growth plate cartilage fuses in adulthood.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-excess-gh">Causes of excess GH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-excess-gh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>pituitary adenomas or hyperplasia - 95% of pts with acromegaly have pituitary adenoma</li>
<li>Hypothalamic tumors- increased GHRH</li>
<li>Ectopic GHRH from tumors- ca lung, pancreas</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-due-to-excess-of-gh-igf-i">Clinical features due to excess of GH/IGF-I<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-due-to-excess-of-gh-igf-i" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Soft tissue swelling and enlargement of extremities</li>
<li>Increase in ring and/or shoe size</li>
<li>Hyperhidrosis (excessive sweating)</li>
<li>Coarsening of facial features</li>
<li>Prognathism (big jaws), widened space between incisor teeth</li>
<li>Macroglossia</li>
<li>Arthritis</li>
<li>Bilateral carpal tunnel syndrome</li>
<li>Increased incidence of obstructive sleep apnea - 60% of pts</li>
<li>Increased incidence of glucose intolerance (80-90%) or frank diabetes mellitus - in 25% of pts, hypertension, and cardiovascular</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypo-secretion-of-anterior-pituitary-hormones">Hypo secretion of anterior pituitary hormones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypo-secretion-of-anterior-pituitary-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pituitary-dwarfism">Pituitary dwarfism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pituitary-dwarfism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is caused by severe deficiency of GH, and possibly of other hormones, in childhood.</li>
<li>The condition may be due to genetic abnormality or a tumor.</li>
<li>Other causes of isolated GH deficiency are abnormalities of GH secreting cells, end organ unresponsiveness to GH and consequently a deficiency of circulating growth factors—ie growth hormone</li>
</ul>
<p>This is a 100% plan
Insensitivity syndrome or L-gren-dwarfism</p>
<p>Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs">Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The individual is of small stature but is normally proportioned and cognitive development is not affected.</li>
<li>Puberty is delayed and there may be episodes of hypoglycaemia.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyposecretion-of-anterior-pituitary-hormones">Hyposecretion of anterior pituitary hormones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyposecretion-of-anterior-pituitary-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The number of hormones involved and the extent of hyposecretion varies.</li>
<li>Panhypopituitarism is the absence of all anterior pituitary hormones.</li>
<li>Causes of hyposecretion include:</li>
<li>tumours of the hypothalamus or pituitary</li>
<li>trauma, usually caused by fractured base of skull, or surgery</li>
<li>pressure caused by a tumour adjacent to the pituitary gland, e.g. glioma, meningioma</li>
<li>infection, e.g. meningitis, encephalitis, syphilis</li>
<li>ischaemic necrosis</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Depends on the hormone lost</li>
<li>Acute s/s with pituitary apoplexy- pt presents with acute features of headaches, confusion, nuchal rigidity (neck stiffness).</li>
<li>Pts with sheehans present with inability to lactate in the postpartum period.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis-assay-hormone-level">Diagnosis- assay hormone level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-assay-hormone-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-the-posterior-pituitary">Disorders of the posterior pituitary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-the-posterior-pituitary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diabetes insipidus</li>
<li>relatively rare condition usually caused by <strong>hyposecretion of ADH</strong> due to damage to the hypothalamus by, for example, trauma, tumour or encephalitis.</li>
<li>Occasionally it occurs when the <strong>renal tubules fail to respond to ADH</strong>.</li>
<li>Water reabsorption by the renal tubules is impaired, leading to excretion of excessive amounts of dilute urine, often more than 10 lt daily, causing dehydration and extreme thirst (polydipsia).</li>
<li>Water balance is disturbed unless fluid intake is greatly increased to compensate for excess losses.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCDS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-adh">Functions of ADH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-adh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Regulates extracellular fluid volume by affecting renal handling of water → reduce free water clearance.</li>
<li>vasoconstrictor &amp; pressor agent (name "vasopressin").</li>
<li>Decreased urine formation (hence, the antidiuretic action of "antidiuretic hormone").</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stimulation-of-adh-secretion">Stimulation of ADH secretion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stimulation-of-adh-secretion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Increase in plasma osmolality / cellular dehydration) is the most important stimulus - detected by hypothalamic osmoreceptors.</li>
<li>Hypovolemia or decreased central venous pressure → decreased firing of atrial stretch receptors leading to increase in ADH release.</li>
<li>Hypovolemia stimulates renin secretion and angiotensin formation. Angiotensin II also stimulates thirst and ADH secretion</li>
<li>Other NIA MEDICAL TRAINING ADH RESERVE include nausea, pain and surgery</li>
</ol>
<p>SUNYI YU BEDIEN BEFOREYARD CHINESE BIOLOGICAL SOCIETY BETER Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NRES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="osmoregulation-of-adh-release">Osmoregulation of ADH release<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#osmoregulation-of-adh-release" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-di">Classification of DI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-di" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Cranial DI: - Deficiency of ADH- complete or partial</li>
<li>Nephrogenic DI: - Renal resistance to ADH</li>
<li>Primary polydipsia: - Polyuria due to excessive drinking (suppressed ADH due to &lt;plasma osmolality)- psychological cause</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-central-d-i">CAUSES OF CENTRAL D.I<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-central-d-i" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A. Familial (5%): Autosomal dominant (ADH gene)
B. DIDMOAD syndrome (DI, DM, optic atrophy, deafness)
C. Acquired:
i. Trauma (head injury, hypothalamic/pituitary surgery)
ii. Tumors (craniopharyngiomas, pituitary mets)
iii. Inflammatory conditions (sarcoidosis, TB, histiocytosis, lymphocytic hypophysitis)
iv. Infections (meningitis, encephalitis)
V. Vascular (Sheehans, Sickle cell disease)</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-nephrogenic-d-i">CAUSES OF NEPHROGENIC D.I<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-nephrogenic-d-i" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A. Familial:
i. X-linked recessive (vasopressin receptor gene)
ii. Autosomal recessive (acquaporin-2 gene)</p>
<p>B. Acquired:-
i. Drugs (lithium)
ii. Metabolic (hypokalemia, hypercalcemia)
iii. Chronic renal disease (obstructive uropathy)
iv. Systemic disorders e.g amyloidosis</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-presentation">CLINICAL PRESENTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Adults: - polyuria, nocturia, thirst</li>
<li>Children: - polyuria, enuresis, and failure to thrive</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="patient-evaluation">PATIENT EVALUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Careful history. Confirm large urine output.</li>
<li>Exclude hyperglycemia (DM), hypokalemia, hypercalcemia and significant renal disease</li>
<li>Measure electrolytes + plasma and urine osmolality</li>
<li>Water deprivation test</li>
<li>MRI of hypothalamus and pituitary - CDI is suspected.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The objectives of therapy are
(1) to replace ADH (which is usually a long-term therapeutic program),
(2) to ensure adequate fluid replacement, and
(3) to identify and correct the underlying cause</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-of-di">Treatment of DI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-di" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The treatment of choice is synthetic, long-acting ADH analogue (Desmopressin) {intranasal spray (5-100 mcg daily); parenteral injection (0.1-2.0 mcg daily); or oral (100-1000 mcg daily), in divided doses. }</li>
<li>Dilutional hyponatremia is the most serious potential adverse effect.</li>
<li>Primary polydipsia(PPD) - Treat underlying cause. Reduced fluid intake is only tx</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<ul>
<li>A thiazide diuretic to deplete sodium and increase renal water reabsorption</li>
<li>Restriction of salt and protein intake</li>
</ul>

<p>Here 9.4 Negative feedback regulation of secretion of hormones by the anterior lobe of the pituitary gland.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="negative-feedback">Negative Feedback<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#negative-feedback" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Negative feedback is the primary mechanism through which your endocrine system maintains homeostasis</li>
<li>Secretion of a specific hormone is turned on or off by specific physiological changes (similar to a thermostat)</li>
<li>EXAMPLE: plasma glucose levels and insulin</li>
</ul>
<p>ENSDOG

Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-the-endocrine-system">Functions of the Endocrine System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Controls the processes involved in movement and physiological equilibrium</li>
<li>Includes all tissues or glands that secrete hormones into the blood</li>
<li>Secretion of most hormones is regulated by a negative feedback system</li>
<li>The number of receptors for a specific hormone can be altered to meet the body’s demand</li>
</ul>

<li>Lipid soluble</li>
<li>Diffuse through cell membranes</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nonsteroid-hormones">Nonsteroid Hormones:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nonsteroid-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Not lipid soluble</li>
<li>Received by receptors external to the cell membrane</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hormone-actions">Hormone Actions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormone-actions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>“Lock and Key” approach: describes the interaction between the hormone and its specific receptor.</li>
<li>Receptors for nonsteroid hormones are located on the cell membrane</li>
<li>Receptors for steroid hormones are found in the cell’s cytoplasm or in its nucleus</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="steroid-hormones">Steroid Hormones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steroid-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pass through the cell membrane</li>
<li>Binds to specific receptors</li>
<li>Then enters the nucleus to bind with the cells DNA which then activates certain genes (Direct gene activation).</li>
<li>mRNA is synthesized in the nucleus and enters the cytoplasm and promotes protein synthesis for:</li>
<li>Enzymes as catalysts</li>
<li>Tissue growth and repair</li>
<li><strong>RENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
QS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nonsteroid-hormones">Nonsteroid Hormones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nonsteroid-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>React with specific receptors outside the cell</li>
<li>This triggers an enzyme reaction with lead to the formation of a second messenger (cAMP).</li>
<li>cAMP can produce specific intracellular functions:</li>
<li>Activates cell enzymes</li>
<li>Change in membrane permeability</li>
<li>Promote protein synthesis</li>
<li>Change in cell metabolism</li>
<li>Stimulation of cell secretions</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="number-of-receptors">Number of Receptors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#number-of-receptors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Down-regulation</strong>: is the decrease of hormone receptors which decreases the sensitivity to that hormone</li>
<li><strong>Up-regulation</strong>: is the increase in the number of receptors which causes the cell to be more sensitive to a particular hormone</li>
</ul>

<p>The endocrine system consists of three major components</p>
<ul>
<li>glands, which are specialized cell clusters or organs</li>
<li>hormones, which are chemical substances secreted by glands in response to stimulation</li>
<li>receptors, which are protein molecules that trigger specific physiologic changes in a target cell in response to hormonal stimulation.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-the-thyroid-gland">Disorders of the thyroid gland<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-the-thyroid-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These fall into three main categories:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>abnormal secretion of thyroid hormones (T3 and T4)</li>
<li>causing hyperthyroidism (thyrotoxicosis) or hypothyroidism (cretinism, myoxedema)</li>
<li>goitre – simple, malignant</li>
<li>Tumours-adenoma, carcinoma</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Abnormal thyroid function may arise not only from thyroid disease but also from disorders of the pituitary or hypothalamus; insufficient dietary iodine impairs thyroid hormone production.</li>
<li>The main effects are caused by an abnormally high or low basal metabolic rate.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyperthyroidism-thyrotoxicosis">Hyperthyroidism- thyrotoxicosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyperthyroidism-thyrotoxicosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Most common endocrine disease</li>
<li>Females &gt; Males – 8 : 1</li>
<li>Often unsuspected and grossly under diagnosed</li>
<li>arises as the body tissues are exposed to excessive levels of T3 and T4.</li>
<li>The main effects are due to increased basal metabolic rate. In older adults, cardiac failure is another common consequence as the ageing heart must work harder to deliver more blood and nutrients to the hyperactive body cells.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCI</p>
<p>The most common forms of hyperthyroidism include</p>
<ol>
<li>diffuse toxic goiter (Graves disease),</li>
<li>toxic multinodular goiter (Plummer disease),</li>
<li>toxic adenoma.</li>
</ol>
<p>Together with subacute thyroiditis, these conditions constitute 85-90% of all causes of thyrotoxicosis</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The hypermetabolic effect of thyrotoxicosis affects every organ system.</li>
<li>Thyroid hormone is made in the thyroid but travels via the circulation to reach every cell in the body.</li>
<li>Thyroid hormone is necessary for normal growth and development, and it regulates cellular metabolism.</li>
<li>Excess thyroid hormone causes an increase in the metabolic rate that is associated with increased total body heat production and cardiovascular activity (increased heart contractility, heart rate, vasodilation).</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<ul>
<li>The major symptoms of thyrotoxicosis include palpitation, nervousness, sweating, hyperdefecation, and heat intolerance.</li>
<li>Women often note a reduction in menstrual flow or oligomenorrhea.</li>
<li>Common signs of thyrotoxicosis include weight loss despite increased appetite, lid lag and stare, sinus tachycardia, atrial fibrillation or high output failure (in elderly individuals), fine tremor, and muscle weakness.</li>
<li>Thyrotoxicosis leads to an apparent increase in sympathetic nervous system symptoms, including nervousness, stare, tremor, and tachycardia</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pulsation of the thyroid gland due to increased blood flow to the gland.</li>
<li>Enlarged thyroid gland</li>
<li>Increase serum T4</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="graves-disease-graves-thyroiditis">Graves' disease- Graves' thyroiditis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#graves-disease-graves-thyroiditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>=Diffuse toxic goiter</p>
<ul>
<li>this condition accounts for 75% of cases of hyperthyroidism.</li>
<li>It affects more women than men and may occur at any age, being most common between the ages of 30 and 50 years.</li>
<li>It is an autoimmune disorder in which an antibody that mimics the effects of TSH is produced, causing:</li>
<li>increased release of T3 and T4 and signs of hyperthyroidism</li>
<li>goitre (visible enlargement of the gland, the antibody stimulates thyroid growth</li>
<li>exophthalmos in many cases.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chronic-thyroiditis-hashimoto-s-disease">CHRONIC THYROIDITIS (HASHIMOTO'S DISEASE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-thyroiditis-hashimoto-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Chronic thyroiditis, which occurs most frequently in women between 30 and 50 years old, has been termed Hashimoto’s disease, or chronic lymphocytic thyroiditis;</li>
<li>its diagnosis is based on the histologic appearance of the inflamed gland.</li>
<li>In contrast to acute thyroiditis, the chronic forms are usually not accompanied by pain, pressure symptoms, or fever, and thyroid activity is usually normal or low rather than increased.</li>
<li>Cell-mediated immunity may play a significant role in the pathogenesis of chronic thyroiditis, and there may be a genetic predisposition to it.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<ul>
<li>If untreated, the disease runs a slow, progressive course, leading eventually to hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>The objective of treatment is to reduce the size of the thyroid gland and prevent hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>Thyroid hormone therapy is prescribed to reduce thyroid activity and the production of thyroglobulin.</li>
<li>If hypothyroid symptoms are present, thyroid hormone therapy is prescribed. Surgery may be required if pressure symptoms persist</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="exophthalmos">Exophthalmos.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exophthalmos" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is protrusion of the eyeballs that gives the appearance of staring, which is due to the deposition of excess fat and fibrous tissue behind the eyes</li>
<li>it is often present in Graves’ disease.</li>
<li>Effective treatment of hyperthyroidism does not completely reverse exophthalmos, although it may lessen after 2–3 years.</li>
<li>In severe cases the eyelids become retracted and may not completely cover the eyes during blinking and sleep, leading to drying of the conjunctiva and predisposing to infection.</li>
<li>It does not occur in other forms of hyperthyroidism.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="enlarged-thyroid-gland-in-goitre">Enlarged thyroid gland in goitre.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#enlarged-thyroid-gland-in-goitre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="toxic-nodular-goitre-plummer-disease">Toxic nodular goitre = Plummer disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toxic-nodular-goitre-plummer-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In this condition one or two nodules of a gland that is already affected by goitre become active and secrete excess T3 and T4 causing the effects of hyperthyroidism.</li>
<li>It is more common in women than men and after middle age.</li>
<li>As this condition affects an older age group than Graves’ disease, arrhythmias and cardiac failure are more common.</li>
<li>Exophthalmos does not occur in this condition.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypothyroidism">Hypothyroidism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypothyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This condition is prevalent in older adults and is five times more common in females than males.</li>
<li>Deficiency of T3 and T4 in adults results in an abnormally low metabolic rate and other effects.</li>
<li>There may be accumulation of mucopolysaccharides in the subcutaneous tissues causing swelling (non-pitting oedema), especially of the face, hands, feet and eyelids (myxoedema).</li>
<li>The commonest causes are autoimmune thyroiditis,</li>
</ul>

<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>00138</p>
<ul>
<li>interventions, e.g. antithyroid drugs, surgical removal of thyroid tissue or ionising radiation.</li>
<li>Autoimmune thyroiditis. The most common cause of acquired hypothyroidism is Hashimoto's disease.</li>
<li>It is more common in women than men and, like Graves' disease, an organ-specific autoimmune condition.</li>
<li>Autoantibodies that react with thyroglobulin and thyroid gland cells develop and prevent synthesis and release of thyroid hormones causing hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>Goitre is sometimes present.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types">Types<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Primary/ thyroidal hypothyroidism- Caused by thyroidal problems</li>
<li>Central hypothyroidism- caused by failure of the pituitary, hypothalamus or both</li>
<li>Secondary/ pituitary hypothyroidism- caused by pituitary problems</li>
<li>Tertiary/ hypothalamic hypothyroidism- caused by problems with hypothalamus</li>
<li>Cretinism- Thyroid deficiency at birth: foetal or neonatal</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Congenital hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>This is a profound deficiency or absence of thyroid hormones that becomes evident a few weeks or months after birth.</li>
<li>Hypothyroidism is endemic in parts of the world where the diet is severely deficient in iodine and contains insufficient for synthesis of T3 and T4.</li>
<li>Absence of thyroid hormones results in profound impairment of growth and cognitive development.</li>
<li>Unless treatment begins early in life, cognitive impairment is permanent and the individual typically has disproportionately short limbs, a large protruding tongue, coarse dry skin, poor abdominal muscle tone and, often, an umbilical hernia.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
KENYA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="simple-goitre">Simple goitre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#simple-goitre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>This is enlargement of the thyroid gland without signs of hyperthyroidism. It is caused by a relative lack of T3 and T4 and the low levels stimulate secretion of TSH resulting in hyperplasia of the thyroid gland</li>
<li>Sometimes the extra thyroid tissue is able to maintain normal hormone levels but if not, hypothyroidism develops.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pth">PTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>primary regulator of calcium - Maintain extracellular (ECF) calcium concentration within a narrow range.</li>
<li>Directly:-</li>
<li>☑ Bone - induces calcium resorption</li>
<li>☑ Kidney - incr calcium reabsorption</li>
<li>Indirectly:</li>
<li>☑ Intestine: - enhances GI absorption via 1,25-dihydroxyvitamin D [1,25(OH)₂D] hormone (from kidney).</li>
</ul>
<p>parathyroid hormone (PTH), which is the physiology. PTH acts directly on bone, where it induces calcium resorption, and on the kidney, where it enhances calcium reabsorption and synthesis of 1,25-dihydroxyvitamin D [1,25(OH)₂D], a hormone that increases gastrointestinal calcium absorption. Serum PTH levels are tightly regulated by a negative feedback loop.</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="renal-effect-of-pth">Renal effect of PTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#renal-effect-of-pth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Inhibition of phosphate transport (proximal tubule),
☑ Augmentation of calcium reabsorption (distal tubule)
☑ Stimulation of the renal 25(OH)D-1α-hydroxylase</p>
<p>NB :- High calcium levels suppresses PTH secretion.</p>
<p>The homeostatic role of the hormone can preserve calcium concentration in blood at the cost of bone demineralization.</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physiologic-effects-of-hypocalcemia">Physiologic effects of hypocalcemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiologic-effects-of-hypocalcemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>incr secretion of PTH- in turn</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Increases the rate of dissolution of bone mineral, thereby incr the flow of calcium from bone into blood;</li>
<li>Reduces the renal clearance of calcium filtered</li>
<li>Increases the efficiency of calcium absorption in the intestine by stimulating the production of 1,25(OH)₂D.</li>
</ol>
<p>Immediate control of blood calcium is due to PTH effects on bone and, to a lesser extent, on renal calcium clearance</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyperparathyroidism">hyperparathyroidism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyperparathyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Increased PTH secretion leading to hypercalcemia and hypophosphatemia.</li>
<li>Incidence 27/100,000</li>
<li>Prevalence women &gt;60 years more than 1%</li>
<li>characterised by high blood calcium levels (hypercalcaemia) and is usually caused by a benign parathyroid tumour which secretes high levels of parathormone (PTH).</li>
<li>This results in release of calcium from bones, raising blood calcium levels. The effects may include:</li>
<li>polyuria and polydipsia</li>
<li>formation of renal calculi</li>
<li>anorexia and constipation</li>
<li>muscle weakness</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypoparathyroidism">Hypoparathyroidism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypoparathyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Parathyroid hormone (PTH) deficiency causes hypocalcaemia, i.e. abnormally low blood calcium levels, and is much rarer than hyperparathyroidism.</li>
<li>There is reduced absorption of calcium from the small intestine and less reabsorption from bones and glomerular filtrate.</li>
<li>Low blood calcium causes:</li>
<li>tetany</li>
<li>anxiety</li>
<li>paraesthesia</li>
<li>grand mal seizures</li>
<li>in some cases, cataracts and brittle nails.</li>
<li>Causes of hypoparathyroidism include damage to or removal of the glands during thyroidectomy, ionizing radiation, development of autoantibodies to PTH and parathyroid cells, and congenital abnormalities.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>^{}[]</p>

Glucocorticoids ('steroids')<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-glucocorticoids-steroids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anti-inflammatory-antiallergic-effects-of-glucocorticoids">Anti-inflammatory &amp; Antiallergic Effects of Glucocorticoids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anti-inflammatory-antiallergic-effects-of-glucocorticoids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Glucocorticoids inhibit the inflammatory response to tissue injury.</li>
<li>The glucocorticoids also suppress manifestations of allergic disease that are due to the release of histamine from tissues.</li>
<li>Large doses of exogenous glucocorticoids inhibit ACTH secretion to the point that severe adrenal insufficiency can be a dangerous problem when therapy is stopped.</li>
<li>An additional action that combats local inflammation is inhibition of phospholipase</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NED</p>
<ul>
<li>This reduces the release of arachidonic acid from tissue phospholipids and consequently reduces the formation of leukotrienes, thromboxanes, prostaglandins, and prostacyclin</li>
<li>Large doses of glucocorticoids inhibit growth, decrease growth hormone secretion, and decrease TSH secretion.</li>
<li>During fetal life, glucocorticoids accelerate the maturation of surfactant in the lungs</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-the-adrenal-cortex">Disorders of the adrenal cortex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-the-adrenal-cortex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypersecretion of glucocorticoids (Cushing’s syndrome)</li>
<li>Cortisol is the main glucocorticoid hormone secreted by the adrenal cortex.</li>
<li>Causes of hypersecretion include:</li>
<li>hormone-secreting adrenal tumours</li>
<li>hypersecretion of adrenocorticotropic hormone (ACTH) by the anterior pituitary</li>
<li>abnormal secretion of ACTH by a non-pituita tumour, e.g. bronchial or pancreatic tumour.</li>
<li>Prolonged therapeutic use of systemic ACTH or glucocorticoids is another cause of Cushing’s syndrome where high blood levels arise from drug therapy.</li>
</ul>
<p>Hypersecretion of cortisol exaggerates its physiological effects</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCI</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-mineralocorticoids">2. Mineralocorticoids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-mineralocorticoids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Aldosterone - main mineralocorticoid.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Involved in maintaining water and electrolyte balance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It stimulates the reabsorption of sodium (Na+), retention of water and excretion of potassium (K+) in the urine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Regulates blood volume and blood pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blood potassium levels is accompanied by retention of water regulate aldosterone secretion, When raised more aldosterone is secreted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Angiotensin also stimulates the release of aldosterone.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-mineralocorticoids">Effects of mineralocorticoids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-mineralocorticoids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action">Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Aldosterone and other steroids with mineralocorticoid activity increase the reabsorption of Na⁺ from the urine, sweat, saliva, and the contents of the colon.</li>
<li>Thus, mineralocorticoids cause retention of Na⁺ in the ECF.</li>
<li>This expands ECF volume.</li>
<li>In the kidneys, they act primarily on the <strong>principal cells (P cells)</strong> of the collecting ducts</li>
<li>Under the influence of aldosterone, increased amounts of Na⁺ are in effect exchanged for K⁺ and H⁺ in the renal tubules, producing a K⁺ diuresis and an increase in urine acidity.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypersecretion-of-mineralocorticoids">Hypersecretion of mineralocorticoids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypersecretion-of-mineralocorticoids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Excess aldosterone affects kidney function, with consequences elsewhere:</li>
<li>excessive reabsorption of sodium chloride and water, causing increased blood volume and hypertension</li>
<li>excessive excretion of potassium, causing hypokalaemia, which leads to cardiac arrhythmias, alkalosis, syncope and muscle weakness.</li>
<li>Primary hyperaldosteronism is due to excessive secretion of mineralocorticoids, independent of the renin-angiotensin-aldosterone system. It is usually caused by a tumour affecting only one adrenal gland.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<ul>
<li>Secondary hyperaldosteronism is caused by overstimulation of normal glands by the excessively high blood levels of renin and angiotensin that result from low renal perfusion or low blood sodium.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-angiotensin-ii-renin">Effects of Angiotensin II &amp; Renin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-angiotensin-ii-renin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The angiotensin II is formed in the body from angiotensin I, which is liberated by the action of renin on circulating angiotensinogen</li>
<li>Renin is secreted from the juxtaglomerular cells that surround the renal afferent arterioles as they enter the glomeruli</li>
<li>Aldosterone secretion is regulated via the renin-angiotensin system in a feedback fashion</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<ul>
<li>A drop in ECF volume or intra-arterial vascular volume leads to a reflex increase in renal nerve discharge and decreases renal arterial pressure.</li>
<li>Both changes increase renin secretion, and the angiotensin II formed by the action of the renin increases the rate of secretion of aldosterone.</li>
<li>The aldosterone causes Na⁺ and, secondarily, water retention, expanding ECF volume and shutting off the stimulus that initiated increased renin secretion</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>BUREAU VERITAS 1828</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>sex hormones (androgens).</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>that exert minor effects on reproductive function.</li>
<li>Androgens are the hormones that exert masculinizing effects, and they promote protein anabolism and growth</li>
<li>Testosterone from the testes is the most active androgen, and the adrenal androgens have less than 20% of its activity</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<ul>
<li>Of these, the mineralocorticoids and the glucocorticoids are necessary for survival.</li>
<li>Adrenocortical secretion is controlled primarily by ACTH from the anterior pituitary,</li>
<li>but mineralocorticoid secretion is also subject to independent control by circulating factors, of which the most important is angiotensin II, a peptide formed in the bloodstream.</li>
<li>The formation of angiotensin is in turn dependent on renin secreted by the kidneys.</li>
</ul>

<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<ul>
<li>Produces the catecholamines</li>
<li>epinephrine, norepinephrine, and dopamine</li>
<li>In humans, 90% of the cells are the epinephrine-secreting type and 10% are the norepinephrine- secreting type.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cushing-s-disease-syndrome">Cushing's Disease/Syndrome<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cushing-s-disease-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
